  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_84fd577a-38ce-4671-b67d-f1dfddc3cdab'
      });
    }

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer565118421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3606640585834071167"><blockquote>
  <i>His eyes drank me in. Oh, the Evanness of it all, how he gulps down my presence like a guy stumbling upon an oasis in the desert.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>What happened to this series?</b><br/><br/>I was one of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_' title='The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The 5th Wave</a>'s biggest fans, singing its praises to everyone who would listen. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131484.The_Infinite_Sea__The_5th_Wave___2_' title='The Infinite Sea (The 5th Wave, #2) by Rick Yancey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Infinite Sea</a> wasn't as strong for me, but that too was an enjoyable experience because I just clicked so much with Yancey's writing. This conclusion was a struggle to finish.<br/><br/>As much as I loved the first book, I'm not going to pretend this ser</span>
  <span id="freeText3606640585834071167" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>His eyes drank me in. Oh, the Evanness of it all, how he gulps down my presence like a guy stumbling upon an oasis in the desert.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>What happened to this series?</b><br /><br />I was one of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_" title="The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The 5th Wave</a>'s biggest fans, singing its praises to everyone who would listen. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131484.The_Infinite_Sea__The_5th_Wave___2_" title="The Infinite Sea (The 5th Wave, #2) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Infinite Sea</a> wasn't as strong for me, but that too was an enjoyable experience because I just clicked so much with Yancey's writing. This conclusion was a struggle to finish.<br /><br />As much as I loved the first book, I'm not going to pretend this series is something it isn't. An alien takeover story is not exactly original, Cassie Sullivan is not Katniss Everdeen, and there are some plot decisions that don't quite add up. But, that being said, I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_" title="The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The 5th Wave</a> was so good for one big reason: <b>atmosphere</b>.<br /><br />I didn't even realize the importance of atmosphere until I read that book. Yancey enthused every page with a deep level of distrust. It was eerie, compelling and it forced you to look over your own shoulder. It was this, more than anything else, that pulled me so deeply inside the book.<br /><br />Here, that whole atmosphere just... disappears. Completely stops existing. That creeping, beautiful style of storytelling has been replaced with gems like this:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>There’s been a shitload of huh? moments since the Others came, but this one has gotta be the huh-est of them all.</i>
</blockquote><br />I've also seen lots of people talking about the ending, which is partly why I kept forcing myself through. However, though dramatic, it's really easy to predict. Arguably, it's the only thing that could have happened to avoid a forced ending where everyone holds hands and walks off into the sunset. I doubt anyone who's read a few other popular YA series will be surprised.<br /><br />But the worst thing about this book is the thing that's been niggling at the back of my mind throughout the entire trilogy - Cassie and Evan. They are so annoying. <b>SO ANNOYING</b>. Though where it was once masked by that writing and atmosphere I talked about, here it becomes reminiscent of New Adult romance novels:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>My hands roamed his body, an undiscovered country, which henceforth I shall call Evanland. Hills and valleys, desert plains and forest glens, the landscape pockmarked with the scars of battle, criss-crossed by fault lines and unexpected vistas. And I am Cassie the Conquistador: The more territory I conquer, the more I want. <br />***<br />My face is hot. I’m thinking of the night I landed on the shores of Evanland and planted my flag upon that sculpted beach.</i>
</blockquote><br />If you're a bit confused what the hell is happening - yes, they are having sex. <b>Did anyone actually read this book through and hear how that sounded before sending it to print?</b><br /><br />Between Cassie's disdain for the overtly sexual Grace and her constant descriptions of Evan's sexy arms and eyes - <i>Tears welled in his eyes. It was like watching chocolate melt</i> - she was insufferable. <br /><br />The saddest thing is that I really did love the first book, and even the second wasn't bad. It's not the kind of series where you can just read one book and be satisfied either - lots of questions are left unanswered. And honestly, viewing the series as a whole, I don't know that it's worth it.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3606640585834071167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1011202017" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1011202017" />
    <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway"><img alt="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456070558p2/32524334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1011202017?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway">Nina (Every Word A Doorway)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011202017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13894347129534092818"><b><i>The Last Star</i> was one of my most anticipated releases of 2016. No one is more saddened than me that 1) this book was a disappointment, and 2) I can’t even lie to myself about how disappointing it was. Hence, the 2.5 stars. Ben Parish was my silver lining, as the Par(r)ishs always are.</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Life is a circle bound by fear. The fear of the predator. The fear of the prey. Without fear, life would not exist.</i>
</blockquote><br/>This is a very detailed review, so beware of minor spoilers. All the major ones are tagged as su</span>
  <span id="freeText13894347129534092818" style="display:none"><b><i>The Last Star</i> was one of my most anticipated releases of 2016. No one is more saddened than me that 1) this book was a disappointment, and 2) I can’t even lie to myself about how disappointing it was. Hence, the 2.5 stars. Ben Parish was my silver lining, as the Par(r)ishs always are.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Life is a circle bound by fear. The fear of the predator. The fear of the prey. Without fear, life would not exist.</i>
</blockquote><br>This is a very detailed review, so beware of minor spoilers. All the major ones are tagged as such.<br><br><b>The characters: ☆☆☆</b><br><br>☛ Cassie<br>Never in my life have I picked up a final instalment only to realize that the main character sounded 100% different than in the previous books. What happened to one of my favourite sarcastic, kick-ass heroines in YA literature? I was completely baffled, still am. Granted, we waited over 18 months for this book. A lot can happen in 18 months. I’m not the same person I was when I read the previous books, but this was a major case of OOC, people. Cassie’s mind was not a nice place to be for a reader. Her endless thoughts were dull, repetitive, without any substance, aaand a little bonkers (see her quote about flags). The sass was limited to a few cranky remarks. This was not the Cassie I remembered, the Cassie who infiltrated an alien fortress to rescue her little brother. This was garbage (see The Romance for reference). <br><blockquote>
  <i>There are times I hate my own brain.</i>
</blockquote> You and me both, girl. <br><br>For a majority of the book, her thoughts circled endlessly around Evan, and Evan, and Evan, and maybe aliens, but mostly Evan. But somewhere towards the climax, there was this one paragraph where I finally wanted to clap her on the shoulder. <br><blockquote>
  <i>My place is with Sam; it’s always been with Sam. Sam is my raison d’être. Not some delusional Ohio farm boy crazy all the way down to the bottom of his bones.</i>
</blockquote><br>I’m a family person through and through, and I would always choose my baby brother over a crush I met a few weeks ago. Teenage romance is this beautiful but short-lived adventure whereas family is a rock-solid fortress. So, for once in this book, I was in accord with Cassie. <br><br>☛ Ben “Zombie”<br>Throughout the book, reading the recycling of Cassie’s dull thoughts, I was glad whenever the name “Ben” showed up beneath the chapter headline. Ben’s POV was engaging, and his mind a place of both tranquillity and sobriety. He got into a lot more trouble than other characters, which meant a lot more action-packed scenes, and who can say No to that in a sci-fi, am I right? What I loved most about Ben, though, was his dark humour and his snarky attitude (well, most of the time), which Evan most often fell victim to, the poor guy. <br><blockquote>
  <i>I drop the rucksack over one shoulder and the rifle over the other. “Buzz Lightyear just told us they’re blowing up the cities.”</i>
</blockquote> Or when he was just being all cute and hopeless.<br><blockquote>
  <i>”[…] My vote is south. Find a source of fresh water, miles from anywhere, as in the middle of nowhere.”<br>“And?” Ringer asks.<br>“And what?”<br>“And what then?”<br>“What then?”<br>“Yes. After we get to nowhere, then what?”<br>Ben lifts a hand. Lets it fall. His mouth curls into smile. He looks so boyishly cute in this moment that I feel like bursting into tears. “There’s five of us. I say we form a band.”</i>
</blockquote> What did piss me off to some extent was how he continuously flirted with both Cassie and Ringer. Like dude, make up your freaking mind. You can’t keep two muffins in the oven. Frankly, I wanted it to be Cassie, because after that ‘Buzz Lightyear’ quote, I was so ready to jump ship (might also have to do with the overwhelming absence of Evan in this instalment but ok...) <br><br>☛ Marika “Ringer”<br>Ringer was the big surprise for me in this book. I didn’t care a lot of her POV in the sequel but, in <i>The Last Star</i>, she had a gripping personal storyline, held my interest, and didn’t take shit from anyone. <br><br>☛ Evan<br>As with <i>The Infinite Sea</i>, Yancey managed to make an interesting character disappear for a majority of the book. Evan was AWOL a lot. Hence, I don’t really have a lot to say about another character I was actually quite fond of in the previous books. I can’t even. <br><br>☛ Sam “Nugget”<br>I wasn’t particularly fond of how Sam was portrayed in <i>The Last Star</i>. The reader barely establishes an emotional connection to Cassie’s 5-yr old brother because his POVs are scarce and limited in their cognitive extension, but I thought that hitherto, Sam had been portrayed quite realistically. Not so in this book. Despite knowing that traumatized children do not think and act rationally, I did not like his damaged relationship with Cassie. Despite knowing that children are capable of pulling triggers, I don’t think it is possible on an anatomical nor a cognitive level for a 5-yr old to construct a wired bomb. Like, please correct me if any of you would like to share your experiences as bomb builders when you were children, but until proven otherwise: No. <br><blockquote>
  <i>My little brother has forgotten the alphabet but he knows how to make bombs. <br>A year ago it was crayons and coloring books, construction paper and Elmer’s glue. Now it’s fuses and blasting caps, wires and black powder. <br>Who wants to read a book when you can blow something up?</i>
</blockquote> Umm, I do?<br><br><b>The plot: ☆☆☆</b><br><br>Plot-wise, the first book was the best of the series. I love it when characters have a goal, a quest, a purpose. In <i>The Last Star</i>, the plot meandered between sitting around and waiting for the sky to explode, and gatecrashing enemy parties. All in all, the plot would have been satisfying if Yancey hadn’t taken the scissors and cut off the ending where I thought shit was about to go down. Don’t get me wrong: Shit hits the fan several times in this book. There is definitely a bit more action than in <i>The Infinite Sea</i> but I really, really wanted to see that ending played out. I hate authors who dangle explosives in front of my face and then throw them in the ocean. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[On the one hand, it makes sense that Cassie sacrifices her life for the purpose of defeating the enemy. Ok, I can live with that. But come on, couldn’t she have taken Evan down with her? The poor dude was just an empty shell in the epilogue and while we know that life isn’t rainbows and daisies, this just felt cruel. And wrong. And heartless. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And Vosch, the antagonist, was a crazy son of a bitch. The most dangerous men are those who do wrong but think they're doing something for the greater good, a lot like Eli in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Vicious___1_" title="Vicious (Vicious, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> (umm, you haven't heard of or read this one yet? Better get onto it). <br><br><b>The writing: ☆☆</b><br><br>I still loved the feel of Yancey’s writing. It would be terrible with fantasy but it works wonderfully for a sci-fi. The apocalyptic feel was definitely there, and yet it lacked some of the spark it had in the previous books. I remember writing down a lot of quotes from <i>The 5th Wave</i> but in <i>The Last Star</i>, I wrote down two. Two quotes that were substantial and made me ponder over them for a while. One of them is the quote at the beginning of this review. The second one was about the absurdity of a teddy bear. <br><blockquote>
  <i>"[…] our highest achievement and the one thing for which I pray we will always be remembered, is stuffing wads of polyester into an anatomically incorrect, cartoonish ideal of one of nature's most fearsome predators for no other reason than to soothe a child."</i>
</blockquote><br><b>The romance: ☆</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>My hands roamed his body, an undiscovered country, which henceforth I shall call Evanland. Hills and valleys, desert plains and forest glens, the landscape pockmarked with scars of battle, crisscrossed by fault lines and unexpected vistas. And I am Cassie the Conquistador: The more territory I conquer, the more I want. <br>His chest heaved: a subterranean quake that rose to the surface like a tsunamic wave.</i>
</blockquote> Desert plains and forest glens? I'm sorry, is this supposed to be sexy? (Also, technically, she would be a conquistadorA, no?). This gave me the creeps. And then, while she’s supposed to worry for Evan’s safety, because the dude has serious martyr issues, she’s thinking this:<br><blockquote>
  <i>My face is hot. I’m thinking of the night I landed on the shores of Evanland and planted my flag upon that sculpted beach.</i>
</blockquote> Excuse me while I go throw up. <br><br>I thought nothing could top SJM’s trembling mountains but this is horrendous. <br><blockquote>
  <i> Ben says something at that point, which I totally miss, because my mind has a way of scolding its own thoughts. Like, how could I be the flag-planter? Shouldn’t that be Evan?</i>
</blockquote> WHO THE FUCK CARES? <br><br>Frankly, if I want to hear a monologue about flags, I’ll watch “Sheldon’s fun with flags” or a documentary on conspiracy theories whether the US has ever really planted a flag on the moon (*drumroll*) but THIS IS EXCRUCIATING. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also, Ben and Ringer? Ehhh, those two did not click with me. They have zero chemistry whatsoever. And for the majority of the book, Ringer was mourning Razor, and then suddenly, she's in love with Ben in the epilogue. Ok. Sure. If you say so. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>The sci-fi element: ☆☆☆</b><br><br>On the one hand, I'm quite satisfied with the conclusion to the sci-fi storyline, a.k.a. alien apocalypse. Yancey created an air of mystery while never fully losing touch with reality, especially after the revelations of the final instalment. On the other hand, I feel like after the previous books, maybe the sci-fi balloon had left some of its air? At times, this felt like a dystopian rather than a sci-fi. <br><br>While there are definitely redeeming qualities, another aspect that factored into this rating were my stratospherically high expections. <i>The 5th Wave</i> was one of my favourite reads in the past years, and after the <i>Infinite Sea</i> hadn't quite reached its epicness, I really expected for Yancey to step up his game for <i>The Last Star</i>. Yes, we do get action. Yes, some characters I still enjoyed. But foremost, the main character, the romance, and the ending weirded me out. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Well, I’m not babysitting while you go all Don Quixote on this.”<br>“You know, making obscure literary references doesn’t impress me.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Well, I’m sad to report that, as with Ben’s literary knowledge, this piece of literature wasn’t particularly impressive, either.<br><br><b>One of the hardest questions I’ve had to answer in the last few weeks: Would you recommend the series? Well, the first book ends with a nerve-wracking cliffhanger, so I wouldn’t try reading <i>The 5th Wave</i> as a standalone. I’ve seen other readers love this final instalment, regarding it as a fitting ending, so yes, if this sounds like it could be your jam, then I would pick up this multiple-POV series about an apocalypse that washed out humanity in 5 waves.</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/the%20big%20bang%20theory" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410424076ra/11105644.gif" alt="the big bang theory photo: If there's an Apocalypse, Good Luck b3d93e07.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>Edit September 2015:<br><br>"Want To Read". Ha! <u>Understatement of the year.</u> <br><br><b>LITERALLY. DYING. TO. READ. THIS.</b> <br><br><br>Except if Yancey dares to kill off any of the important characters (Cassie. Ben. Sam. Ringer. <i>Evan</i>), then I'll probably buy it just for the pleasure of seeing it burn in my backyard. <b>Be warned, Yancey.</b><br><br><br><br>Has anyone else noticed how Yancey picks his book titles from chapter captions of the previous installment? </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13894347129534092818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1134947138" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1134947138" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1134947138?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=badass-females">badass-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134947138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11648773636630770898"><b>This ladies and gentlemen, is how you end a series. I'm freaking speechless.</b> <br/><br/>I have a feeling a lot of people are going to be left feeling this way. This review is going to be hard to write... and seeing as it is the last in a trilogy I'm going to keep it spoiler free.. Going to warn you now, if you don't remember a lot from the first two books please take the time to go back and re-read them! You'll need the information you might have lost. <i>The Last Star</i> is everything I wanted out of a final bo</span>
  <span id="freeText11648773636630770898" style="display:none"><b>This ladies and gentlemen, is how you end a series. I'm freaking speechless.</b> <br><br>I have a feeling a lot of people are going to be left feeling this way. This review is going to be hard to write... and seeing as it is the last in a trilogy I'm going to keep it spoiler free.. Going to warn you now, if you don't remember a lot from the first two books please take the time to go back and re-read them! You'll need the information you might have lost. <i>The Last Star</i> is everything I wanted out of a final book and then some. I got so many of the answers I was looking for. The mystery surrounding the 5th Wave is finally revealed. <br><br><i><b>"If they don't need bodies, they don't need a planet. and if they don't need a planet, why did they come for ours?"</b> </i><br><br><i>The Last Star</i> brings back all the characters you know and love. Giving everything we've been missing over the last year. Since this series is so character driven I was waiting on pin and needles to see how the finale would bring their development. We get a lot more Sammy in this book. Cassie's sweet, loveable, lost in a world of madness brother. We get to really see how being forced to grow up so young really shapes a person and their thoughts. Ringer is still this powerhouse. Still this tough egg that no one can see crack. Now that she's been enhanced she really gets to see what's on the line. That the world isn't just about her. I might have loved her in the first two books, but this one shows there is still so much of her we've never seen. Don't worry though she's still the expressionless genius she was before, but now she's fighting for more than just herself. <br><br><i><b>"I'm coming, you son of a bitch. You wanted to create a human without humanity. Now you're going to get one."</b> </i><br><br>Then we have Evan Walker, the alien everyone loves to hate. All the mystery and guessing about him finally comes forth, perfectly groomed nails and all. He is still so sexy, forward, and so clear. He was my favorite character in the first two books (though he might have taken a step back in the last) everything about this book reminded me why I love him so much. We figured out why he is human, but not. Why he has been so torn, and now what he must do about it. There are some very yummy scenes with him that I've been dying for so that didn't hurt either. Now on to the last two characters, these were the two I was most worried about. Zombie and Cassie. Zombie and his charming smile doesn't disappoint in this series. This book made him. He is the glue that holds everything together. He is the kind of person the end of the world needs. He gives all his heart in this book. He becomes more than this ex jock girl crush he was before the attacks. And Lastly Cassie. Cassiopeia, the sassy, snarky, silver tongued, last human in humanity. She is everything I want out of my female protagonist. Her characters is so realistic. Her thoughts and actions mirror real life. I was scared with the weight of everything this book was going to bring that we weren't going to get the classic Cassie we were begging for, but we did. She still brings all her witty commentary...<br><br><i>
  <b>"Whipped cream in a can. Those cinnamon rolls Mom made every Sunday morning. McDonald's French fries. Bacon. No, bacon was still a possibility. I would just have to find a hog, slaughter it, butcher it, cure the meat, then fry it up. Thinking about the bacon- the potential of bacon- gives me hope. Not all is lost if bacon isn't."</b>
</i><br><br>But she also brings so many emotions and heartache. She by far has the greatest character development in this series. She has come light years from the girl scared in her tent. From the girl who thought she was the last girl on earth. She is a fighter and will stop at nothing to take back the world. She continues to give everything she has in this final book. There is so much more I want to gush about these characters, but I refuse to go any further with them because of spoilers. <br><br>As for the plot of this book... God it had me worried. I'm not going to lie, it's a bit slow at first. It is very Rick Yancey like. It starts out slow, then has you completely baffled about what is going on and who will end up where, it'll twist your mind till it can't take anymore, then hit you dead on with a mind blowing surprise. This is a book that will make you work for the answers you've been seeking, and the battle is worth it. <i>The Last Star </i>just kept peeling back all these layers and everything comes together. This book perfectly ties every book together. It takes pieces from <i>The 5th Wave</i>, and sections of <i>The Infinite Sea </i>and molds them into <i>The Last Star</i>. Most of my time was spent scream WTF is going on... but the ending, Lord the ending. It is everything I wanted. The first three section might have been slower, but they are just setting the table for the last two. There's action, fighting, depth, loss, and love all beautifully crafted in less than 400 pages. <br><a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-HR_p_haztu4/V0GumdTYmGI/AAAAAAAADgY/qAAs6xD8d8cQij4wXiwvJkZLFRPLdHuOgCLcB/s1600/harry.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="133" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463926123ra/19175861.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Rick Yancey has no problems taking bold stroke and this book proves it. He had me laughing, crying, on the edge of my seat, then crying all over again. He has proven that a final book in a series doesn't have to be perfectly neat that they can be messy. That they can be all the things you hate and love mushed together to make this crazy cluster F of a read. I had so many theories about how this would end, and they were all wrong and they were all right. Every little detail down to the title was perfectly woven together to make this masterpiece series complete. <br><br>An out of this world ending to my favorite alien trilogy.<br><br><b> Read this review and others over on my blog<br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> <br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> <br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11648773636630770898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1521813886" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1521813886" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1521813886?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1521813886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14981331563578245055"><i>“She was the mayfly, here for a day, then gone. She was the last star, burning bright in a sea of limitless black.”</i><br/><br/>I read the first two books back-to-back last summer and I absolutely loved them—I think partly because I was binge-watching <b>The Walking Dead</b> at that time and the books reminded me in some way of the show and also because this series is just completely epic.<br/><br/>So when I finished <i>The Infinitive Sea</i> after being in a book-marathoning haze, I couldn’t believe I had to wait <u>a full year</u> to fi</span>
  <span id="freeText14981331563578245055" style="display:none"><i>“She was the mayfly, here for a day, then gone. She was the last star, burning bright in a sea of limitless black.”</i><br><br>I read the first two books back-to-back last summer and I absolutely loved them—I think partly because I was binge-watching <b>The Walking Dead</b> at that time and the books reminded me in some way of the show and also because this series is just completely epic.<br><br>So when I finished <i>The Infinitive Sea</i> after being in a book-marathoning haze, I couldn’t believe I had to wait <u>a full year</u> to find out what would happen next.<br><br>And now here I am finished with the last book with tears in my eyes because THIS WORLD WAS EVERYTHING.<br>I was so scared that I wouldn’t love it quite as much as the first two because it’s been so long (and because I quit watching TWD after season 5— I’m still mad about that season), but I needn’t have worried.<br>I don’t know how, but I forgot how much I loved this series and, thankfully, <i>The Last Star</i> brought it all back. The humor and snarky comments and everything was just right up my ally. I’m still reeling from how good it was.<br>And you know a book is that good when you don’t even pay attention to how many pages you’ve read. (It also helps that Rick writes short chapters, which are my favorite in big books.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464148903i/19202572.jpg" width="440" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464149404i/19202605._SX540_.jpg" width="440" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br><br>The amount of times I gasped throughout this novel were one too many. Every twist and turn came so unexpectedly and there was just so much happening that putting this book down didn’t even cross my mind. Every time I expected a zig, there was a zag, and I just applaud Rick Yancey.<br><br><br><br>A quick recap taken from <a href="http://www.bookseriesrecaps.com" rel="nofollow noopener">bookseriesrecaps.com</a> —The five strange waves of the attack are as follows:<br><br><u>1st wave</u> – a massive electromagnetic pulse (It happened 10 days after satellites captured the first images of the alien mothership nearing Earth.)<br><u>2nd wave</u> – an earthquake, which caused an enormous tsunami (It took out 40% of the Earth’s population, those who lived within 60 miles of a coastline.)<br><u>3rd wave</u> – an awful Ebola-like virus made airborne and spread through bird feces (It wiped out 97% of the people who contracted it.)<br><u>4th wave</u> – intruders planted long ago in human babies (They awakened when the hosts became teenagers, and these infested humans begin to quietly kill any surviving humans. Humans refer to them as Silencers.)<br><u>5th wave</u> – kids taken away from their families and trained as soldiers (They are trained to kill anyone who lights up green, which they think are infested humans but actually are the opposite.)<br><br><br>The first chapter in this book starts out from the point of view of a very creepy priest. I had no idea what to take from that but, as I’ve noticed in this series, everything comes full circle.<br><br><i>“The lights go out, they come back on. The floodwaters roll in, they roll out again. Folks get sick, they get better. Life goes on. That’s true faith, isn’t it?”.</i><br><br>We leave creepy priest for a while to focus on my favorite survival group and the discovery that they have four days left till <i>the end of the world.</i>.<br><br>My mantra throughout this whole journey was that nobody was going to die on my watch. Not Evan not Ben not Sammy or Cassie and certainly not Ringer.<br><br>And speaking of Sam, seeing what a toll the war had taken on him just broke me.<br><br><i>“He crawls into the bed opposite Megan’s and stares at the bare wires and the two dusty metal balls hanging from the ceiling. Megan is watching him, pulling Bear tight against her chest, and her mouth hangs open a little, like the air is running out.<br>He turns his head toward the wall. He doesn’t want Megan to see him cry.<br>He isn’t a baby. He’s a soldier.”</i><br>I'm definitely not crying right now, right?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464149184ra/19202588.gif" width="250" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464149184ra/19202589.gif" width="250" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>In the previous books Cassie’s chapters were my favorite ones but, as Ringer put it, she could be timid but impulsive, naïve but serious, sensitive but flippant.<br>Yet Cassie has this perfectly distinguishable voice with just the right amount of funny, sentimental and, okay, sometimes a bit self-absorbed.<br><br><i>“I have to get this straight. Now. Like, right now.<br><b>This</b> being my head.<br>Four A.M. Jazzed up on too much chocolate (thanks, Grace) and too much Evan Walker. Or not enough Evan Walker. That’s an inside joke, if you can make inside jokes in a private journal. I’ll get to the private parts later. Ha! Another joke. You know you’ve reached a very sad place when the only person who can make you laugh is yourself.”</i><br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464149377ra/19202603.gif" width="250" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464149377ra/19202604.gif" width="250" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Her humor and, surprisingly, Ben’s sarcasm were the icing on the cake for this story.<br><br>I still can’t believe Cassie told Ben about her old-time crush. She as bold as I’ll never be.<br><br><i>“There is something I’d like to say.”<br>“I’m listening.”<br>Looking away. Looking at nothing. Deep breath. Don’t say it, Cass. What’s the point now? There is no point. Maybe that’s something we both need to understand.<br>“I’ve had a crush on you since the third grade,” I whisper. “I wrote your name in notebooks. I drew hearts around it. I decorated it with flowers. Mostly daisies. I had daydreams and dream-dreams, and nobody knew except my best friend. Who is dead. Like everybody else.”</i><br>I had to put down my book for a solid minute because I was laughing so hard. (<b>I still am</b>.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464149614ra/19202617.gif" width="450" height="259" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But on a more serious not, that ending just shattered my reality. It did feel a little rushed, I barely accepted one death when another came around.<br><br>And then Cassie entered Vosch’s pod, which at first I didn’t really get why. Until I did— when she reached into her pocket and fished out the capsule. It was unbearably sad because she went through so much during this series and she didn’t get to have her happy ending with Sammy.<br><br><i>“I am entwined with everything, from mayflies to the farthest star. I have no boundaries, I am limitless, and I open to creation like a flower to the rain.<br>I’m not cold anymore. The arms of the seven billion enfold me.<br>I rise.”</i><br><br>But at the same time I was so damn proud of her for standing up for herself. It’s just such a bittersweet ending to everything.<br>And I know that I’ll cherish this series for a very long time, I seriously cannot wait for what Rick Yancey will write next.<br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>The Last Star</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. <div id="review_1189680273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1189680273" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38522514-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494283297p2/38522514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1189680273?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/38522514-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1189680273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5521978889243503939">Rating: 2.5<br/><br/>The 5th Wave trilogy is over. Unfortunately, as the series went on each book got worse. It's sad to see a book that has so much potential be wasted away due to characterization problems. <br/><br/>Yancey has the tendency to contradict himself. Cassie said she didn't believe in love, Cassie is in love with multiple people. Cassie says she's gonna have sex with one person she truly loves and that she's gonna wait for the right time, Cassie has sex in the heat of the moment with Evan (saying he lo</span>
  <span id="freeText5521978889243503939" style="display:none">Rating: 2.5<br /><br />The 5th Wave trilogy is over. Unfortunately, as the series went on each book got worse. It's sad to see a book that has so much potential be wasted away due to characterization problems. <br /><br />Yancey has the tendency to contradict himself. Cassie said she didn't believe in love, Cassie is in love with multiple people. Cassie says she's gonna have sex with one person she truly loves and that she's gonna wait for the right time, Cassie has sex in the heat of the moment with Evan (saying he loves the "idea" of her). Cassie says she doesn't do sports, Cassie plays soccer. Cassie says she doesn't like Ben, Cassie still fantasizes about him. It's all a big mess. Ringer criticizes Ben for burying Dumbo, Ringer buries the entire squad she kills. <br /><br />Ben in the first book was written so well. My goodness, I loved that boy. In the second book he gets brushed aside. In this book however he becomes a main focus again. But he's different. Ben's perspective is so weird in this book. He's saying things he wouldn't say, he's DUMB! In the second book he was dumb too but in this book he's still dumb which I don't understand since he supposed to be smart! What really bothered me though was this constant joking about his character being based on his mistake with his sister. It's kind of like Yancey treated it like it wasn't a big deal to Ben anymore: "'Like you went back for Sam. Like you didn't go back for-' 'Yes. No. Oh, shit.'" First of all who even says "oh, shit" to something like that? Second of all, why is what happened to his sister something so conversational? Cassie just mentions it like it's nothing. Ben losing his sister marked him in T5W but in this book that driving force, that haunting he had was so irrelevant. I didn't get to read his development and feel his pain. I didn't even feel anything from his relationship with Nugget which was such a driving force for him in T5W and even in TIS. Ben cares more for Nugget than Cassie does and in this book he forgets him multiple times which is so unrealistic. <br /><br />Yancey tries too hard to make each of his characters strange. He relies a lot on making them think about weird things in moments where they shouldn't be. Cassie shouldn't be thinking about her crooked nose and Ringer's perfect nose when she's gonna die. There's no sense of urgency in this book just because there's too much aloofness in each character. Because they're all so weird and random they kind of blend into each other. <br /><br />As for the romance, this book would be better off without it. I find that most of the parts that don't seem right, personality wise, are when they're involving romance. Cassie and Evan will forever be on the worst pairings to ever exist. I never got any sense of love from either of them. Cassie was too confused to even know what love is in relation to Evan. Her confused feelings for Evan put him in front of Sam multiple times which bothered me a lot. Evan on the other hand is completely and utterly obsessed with her which is so creepy. I don't like how Yancey romanticized his obsession with her, especially how she got shot by him. Now, onto the most random pairing ever: Ben and Ringer. What in the world? It's almost like he needed to have a couple at the end and he just shoved Ringer and Ben together. They've been together for 2 whole books and Yancey didn't hint at any attraction or feelings towards either of them. Why not keep it platonic? In fact, he even made Ben look like he cared about Cassie in this last book. He was always touching her face and then suddenly he liked Ringer and was jealous of Razor...? Why didn't Yancey just keep Razor alive considering Ringer was pregnant? And why was she pregnant? All of a sudden this book became so melodramatic. It's like I was watching a soap opera. Of course she's pregnant! <br /><br />All in all, a huge disappointment. I loved the ending for Cassie and the small bits of characterization that underwent when there was NO romance. But the book dragged on and on with forced romance and inconsistent perspectives. The ending and overall meaning of the story was downplayed. It could've been executed a lot better. There was no sense of closure with what the Others wanted and why. They were just there and I guess they were gone? <br /><br />SAVE BEN PARISH 2K15 (Ben is not Ben anymore tbh)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5521978889243503939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1381377673" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1381377673" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36179502-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507346345p2/36179502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1381377673?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/36179502-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1381377673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12819717354142044154"><b>so a couple of things:</b><br/><br/>1. that was <i>depressing as hell</i><br/>2. what the fuck just happened<br/>3. <b>SERIOUSLY WHAT JUST HAPPENED?!</b><br/><br/><b>-S-P-O-I-L-E-R-S-</b><br/><br/>Let me just start off by saying that <b>the first two books in this series were some of my favorite books ever</b>. Not just books I loved, but books that were <i>favorites</i> among the hundreds I've read. If not for some of the actions of certain characters (Evan and Cassie, that's you), I would've given this 1 star.<br/><br/><b>Sad, <i>right</i>?</b><br/><br/>Not only did this book <b>a.)</b> take me a million years </span>
  <span id="freeText12819717354142044154" style="display:none"><b>so a couple of things:</b><br /><br />1. that was <i>depressing as hell</i><br />2. what the fuck just happened<br />3. <b>SERIOUSLY WHAT JUST HAPPENED?!</b><br /><br /><b>-S-P-O-I-L-E-R-S-</b><br /><br />Let me just start off by saying that <b>the first two books in this series were some of my favorite books ever</b>. Not just books I loved, but books that were <i>favorites</i> among the hundreds I've read. If not for some of the actions of certain characters (Evan and Cassie, that's you), I would've given this 1 star.<br /><br /><b>Sad, <i>right</i>?</b><br /><br />Not only did this book <b>a.)</b> take me a million years to read <b>b.)</b> put me to sleep and <b>c.)</b> make me angry, but it also made me partially regret even starting the series. So anyway, gonna list some reasons for disliking this book and <b>THEY'RE SPOILERS</b>, especially number 4, so heads up!<br /><br /><b>1.) Ben and Ringer. </b>Am I the only one who never saw Ben/Zombie's thing for Ringer in the past books? I always thought they were just friends who trusted and respected each other, but I never once saw a romance there.... And suddenly <i>*poof*</i>, Ben's adoration for Ringer pretty much overpowers everything. Both of them were my favorite characters and then suddenly, they weren't. <br /><br /><b>2.) </b>What even was the plot? <i>What actually happened throughout this whole book?</i> There were so many times I just got lost or read without really 'reading', and then had to go back to the beginning of the chapter. And then when I did, I realized: <b>nothing important or interesting happened anyway.</b><br /><br /><b>3.) The god awful 'sex scene' with Cassie and Evan.</b> I shipped them, but I was kind of hoping for Ben and Cassie at the end. I thought it'd be cute since she'd always had a crush on him, you know? I'm okay that they didn't end up together, but Evan and Cassie didn't have to be so weird with each other. <i>*shivers* </i><br /><br /><b>4.) THAT ENDING.</b> Cassie dead, Evan depressed, Sam literally not giving a shit for Cassie, Ben just being there, and Ringer with a baby............................. okay then. I wanted a crazy, mind-blowing finale, and instead <i>I closed my book feeling dead inside.</i> Nice.<br /><br />Overall, yeah I hated it.. <b>but I still think Yancey's a great writer and storyteller.</b> And I definitely do not discourage others from reading the last book or series, because who knows? You may like it.<br /></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=trope-space">trope-space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=imo-expected-smth-better">imo-expected-smth-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=pov-multiple">pov-multiple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1101568284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7989218638767052817"><b>
  <blockquote>2.5 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br/><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br/><a href='http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/06/the-last-star-by-rick-yancey.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br/><br/><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UfXY1veK5K4' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dead Man's Bones – Lose Your Soul</a><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JdUckhF0Zc8' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dikta – Someone, Somewhere</a><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bA1srd_bczs' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mich Gerber ft. Jaël of Lunik – You Remain</a><br/> <br/><b>Genre</b>: apocalyptic, YA<br/><b>Stuff</b>: aliens, humans, the end of the world<br/><b>Fail</b>: lame explanations, the final<br/><b>WOW</b>: Evan and Cassie<br/><b>POV</b>: 1st and 3rd person, multi<br/><b>Love-Geometry</b>: no</span>
  <span id="freeText7989218638767052817" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>2.5 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br><a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/06/the-last-star-by-rick-yancey.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br><br><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UfXY1veK5K4" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Dead Man's Bones – Lose Your Soul</a><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JdUckhF0Zc8" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Dikta – Someone, Somewhere</a><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bA1srd_bczs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Mich Gerber ft. Jaël of Lunik – You Remain</a><br> <br><b>Genre</b>: apocalyptic, YA<br><b>Stuff</b>: aliens, humans, the end of the world<br><b>Fail</b>: lame explanations, the final<br><b>WOW</b>: Evan and Cassie<br><b>POV</b>: 1st and 3rd person, multi<br><b>Love-Geometry</b>: none<br><br><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>"Who needs a 12th System when you have a heart like Cassie Sullivan’s?"</i>
</blockquote><br>Buddy-read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1056331108" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Nastassja</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1377993296" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1508055957" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Vera</a> (who's very busy but she's with us and would finish the book long before the end of the world).<br><br>First of all, <b>SPOILER ALERT</b>. Just close your eyes and run away if you don't want to be spoiled. For the rest of you, let's get the party started.<br><br>I'm sure, many of you haven't read my reviews for the first books in this series, 'cause they were written in Russian only and I was too lazy to translate them. But believe me, I loved <i>
  <b>The 5th Wave</b>
</i> and really liked <i>The Infinite Sea</i>. I was aware of its flaws, but had a hope for logical explanations Yancey could give us later. As long as <b>
  <i>The Last Star</i>
</b> was out of my reach, there was a chance for an epic conclusion. Now I've read it and... WTF?<br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-a_4_HwYqWvM/V10_vhrUNWI/AAAAAAAAAvU/BIx-Gwq-PsMv_DrNwDmotrcvIpgJu7XoQCLcB/s1600/tumblr_o1dg7bcnaE1tqou9go2_1280.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="200" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465798046i/19400837._SX540_.jpg" width="640" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br>Do you see this falling star? That's not a star. Surprise! That's my excitement for this series shortly before it burned in the atmosphere.<br><br><i>
  <b>Now to the reasons.</b>
</i><br><br>Quite every character was <b>OOC</b>. It's like the author forgot what kind of persons they used to be: Cassie lost her wits, Sam was acting like a bitch, Ringer became Mary Sue and Special Snowflake side by side, Ben was him average self only this time he was also sweet upon Ringer and swearing at Sam, Evan was... Evan wasn't. Just wasn't there for the most part of the book.<br><br><b>Cassie</b>. She's been my favorite female-lead with this series from the book #1. Her outer thorns and inner vulnerability dressed up with a good sarcasm were an awesome mix, pus her way to tell the story was the most entertaining among other POVs. <b>
  <i>The Last Star</i>
</b> showed me another Cassie. I was rolling my eyes every time she was speaking or even thinking. I mean,<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"My face is hot. I’m thinking of the night I landed on the shores of Evanland and planted my flag upon that sculpted beach."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Said no girl ever. Even during the apocalyptic time.<br><br>Next to the end Cassie got back to her old self and though the damage was done I liked her better than Ringer the Great.<br><br><b>Ringer</b>. This girl was so irritating: too smart, too special, too beautiful, too everything. She was one of the secondary characters in <i>
  <b>The 5th Wave</b>
</i>, but then people start praising her and in the second book she replaced Cassie on the main female character's throne. That could be okay if in the third installment the central hero was Ben or Evan (why not Evan?!) or even Vosch. But it was Ringer all over again. I hated her attitude. She was such a hypocrite with looking down her nose at people, considering them stupid and judging them non-stop while making mistakes too. The other characters couldn't stop thinking of how brilliant, strong and amazing she was, of her silky hair and porcelain skin. Silky hair... bah. Even Vosch loved her. There were thousands of teens, but he was charmed only by her.<br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-oF_w-8iWPxY/V12-bVvrVMI/AAAAAAAAAwU/pWCU8RsHVbUHx5VIVFrT2dL-JqLz6QjNgCLcB/s1600/specialstatustulips.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="156" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465798046i/19400838.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-oq2p7f_e0yI/V12-3WQ8JQI/AAAAAAAAAwc/uMngULSaBVQ-Z1qFvTdif9y_4Kn2ZMQZgCLcB/s1600/Special.png" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465798046i/19400839.png" width="198" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Ben</b>. Hm... I'm not sure about him. He was charming indeed, but his charms were all about Ringer. I might like how funny and kind he was, even loved him as lone hero: Ben Parrish without cheesy crush on Ringer. But in <i>
  <b>The Last Star</b>
</i> Ben I might like was gone. Also I didn't recognize his way of thoughts and choice of words. <i>Little shit</i>? <i>Son of a bitch</i>? I can't remember him saying something like that toward Sam before. <br><br><b>Sam</b>. This 6 year-old was acting, thinking and feeling as a mature person, which was pretty ridiculous. He was taken by military at the age of 5, had spent in their camp only 2 or 3 months and escaped being a totally different child. I'm talking not about psychotrauma he must to get after such adventures, I'm talking about guns, killings and making bombs. About hatred and his behavior around Cassie. A few weeks in an army-like place can't change you so fundamentally. Zombie became his everything, Ringer became his idol, Meghan became his friend, Cassie became a part of the furniture. How on Earth? For what? Also, Yancey couldn't decide whether Sam did grow up in a record pace or remained a child. One minute he acted as an adult, the other was getting into a fight for his Bear's name with little girl. All in all, I wasn't amused.<br><br><b>Evan</b>. This character made me feel. He was the only "Other" among the rest of the heroes, and while readers already knew the truth about Evan's nature, he wasn't aware of it and still went against 'his own' kind. Why? Because of a mere girl. THAT. That's precisely my favorite type of heroes. I can't relate with martyrs those goals are to save 'em all. But I understand willingness to do anything for a single person. That's a very humanly thing. Also, his character was complicated, he had a conflict within. Why Yancey decided not to develop him better? There was an ocean of potential. Instead we had to endure the same old song about VQP and similar jazz.<br><br><b>Romance</b>. Oh dear God, that was terrific.<br><br>The only couple with real feelings (I mean Cassie and Evan) had nothing in this book, aside from the sorta 'rapping' scene. After that they just went and died. One forever, the other just for while. Yes, deeds are louder than words, sacrifices have more weight than kisses and hugs, but...<br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-aKOOx7VES5k/V13C9pcCokI/AAAAAAAAAws/2hA_bIee8e4woxjFm7CYd6oxOby7NqTdACLcB/s1600/I-see-what-you-did-there-700x560.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465798046i/19400840.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br>Ringer's sob-fest about Razor was lame, repetitive and boring. The pregnancy thing was predictable and unrealistic. One sex-time, a lot of pre-stress, and voila, a baby. Needless to say, the child's survival was fantasy-like. Ringer said that the 12th system protects only its host, it can regenerate your body, but not the embryo or fetus you carry inside. Recalling how badly Ringer was beating during the book, I see no way she could keep the pregnancy. Really.<br><br>Ringer plus Ben was a forced and chemistry-less pairing. She loved Razor and then suddenly 'Only Zombie matters' did happen. He was an adequate guy and then people started to die because Ringer was all he could dream about. He even forgave her deception immediately, 'cause she was bad-ass and beautiful. Ughr...<br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-JkY6LEswPSY/V13FP5xUahI/AAAAAAAAAw4/xJsY0aFyOy4rEwmplJpquXF_Qj0ruBPTQCKgB/s1600/please_die_gratefully-500x535.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465798046i/19400841.jpg" width="297" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br>Okay, we can assume this book wasn't about love, that's why this part of the story was poorly written. But it was! Yancey did say that, not me.<br><br><b>Writing style</b>. There were a few powerful scenes, several smart lines and a couple of feeling-packed pages, but mostly it was a repetitive (VERY REPETITIVE), milk-and-water-ish prose. There were moments for those I'd been waiting since <b>
  <i>The 5th Wave</i>
</b> and they turned out to be rushed or aborted. Yeah, 'cause better to talk about people's cooperation and trust for the 342762876th time with the same words and the same conclusions.<br><br><b>The details</b>. We found out that the Others had music and their true appearance was gross. What else? Nothing else. Their goal was simple, our cure was its match. Love. Unpredictable and unfathomable. Yeah, except it's a biochemical process. Study a psychopath and you'd get what he lacks to be able to love. Also, love IS predictable. Look at Cassie and her devotion for Same, look at Evan and his sacrifices for Cassie. Their reactions WERE predictable. That's I didn't buy that. Love is a good and reasonable excuse in stories about local wars, but not about alien invasions. Moreover, I don't understand why aliens so complicated their task? Vosch said they simply wanted to cleanse the Earth, to reset our ecosystem, that's why they'd started to change human nature, so we could kill one another without their help. Also they were going to bomb all the marks of our civilization. Okay, they could bomb cities without any prelude, make the earthquakes harder, thus tsunami could be higher (like in movie "2012"), and then<br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-r2cbI3ZXto0/V12rvWV6OoI/AAAAAAAAAwE/lWnAczuCgeg7fxr-KaPR0xatlwOfbEpBACLcB/s1600/Tsunami-wave1.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="300" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465798046i/19400842._SX540_.jpg" width="600" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br>Goodbye everything. Duh.<br><br><b>The ending</b>. Cassie died. Somehow it was naturally and fitting (after uploading so many memories into her head, after chemical rain, after Evan's erasing...). But her death wasn't enough, 'cause it was too-much. I mean, there were five main characters (I don't count Meghan) and only one had to die in the end. That's why Cassie's fate seemed too tragic and too unfair. Someone (or two) else had to die as well. And I wasn't impressed with how Yancey described her death. There were so many crooked-nose-thoughts, I might think that Cassie committed suicide instead of sacrificing herself.<br><br>I think Cassie's heroic act didn't safe people. Just gave them a break. What would stop aliens from coming again? They got that the mothership was destroyed and they definitely have another. You're safe as long as no one in the cosmos learns about your existence. People had already blown they cover, that's why Cassie's death wasn't for nothing, but was in vain.<br><br>Also, I hate that now Ringer has a baby named after Cassie, lives with her little brother and school-crush, and had resurrected Evan, 'cause humans have to suffer. Who do you think you are? What did you do aside from charming Vosch with your awfully brooding self? Brought death on Teacup's, Pundcakes's, Dumbo's and Razor's heads with leaving the Hotel.<br><br>My ideal final:<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Three Bens, two Cassies, a couple of Sams, and, of course, the literal duality of Evan Walker."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>No Ringer. No Marika. No porcelain skin.<br><br><b>Overall</b>. WHY OH WHY.<br><br><b>The 5th Wave (Пятая волна):</b><br><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101567961" rel="nofollow noopener">The 5th Wave (Пятая волна)</a> #1/3<br>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101567973" rel="nofollow noopener">The Infinite Sea (Бесконечное море)</a> #2/3<br>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101568284" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Star (Последняя звезда)</a> #3/3</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7989218638767052817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4959018269474251669">The Last Star (The 5th Wave #3), Rick Yancey<br/><br/><b>The Last Star</b> is a young adult science fiction novel written by American author <b>Rick Yancey</b>. It was published on May 24, 2016, by G. P. Putnam's Sons. <br/><br/>The novel is the third and final in The 5th Wave trilogy, preceded by The Infinite Sea. The Last Star concludes the story of 16-year-old Cassiopeia "Cassie" Sullivan battling against the aliens that have invaded Earth. It continues the story from where it left off in The Infinite Sea.<br/><br/>تاریخ نخستین خوانش: </span>
  <span id="freeText4959018269474251669" style="display:none">The Last Star (The 5th Wave #3), Rick Yancey<br /><br /><b>The Last Star</b> is a young adult science fiction novel written by American author <b>Rick Yancey</b>. It was published on May 24, 2016, by G. P. Putnam's Sons. <br /><br />The novel is the third and final in The 5th Wave trilogy, preceded by The Infinite Sea. The Last Star concludes the story of 16-year-old Cassiopeia "Cassie" Sullivan battling against the aliens that have invaded Earth. It continues the story from where it left off in The Infinite Sea.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز نهم ماه دسامبر سال 2016 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: سه گانه موج پنجم - کتاب سوم - آخرین ستاره؛ نویسنده: ریک یانسی؛ برگردان: مهنام عبادی؛ ویراستار: نیما کهندانی؛ تهران، بهداد، 1395؛ شابک: 9786008203131؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 21م<br /><br />عنوانهای کتابهای سه گانه موج پنجم: کتاب اول «موج پنجم»؛ کتاب دوم «دریای بیکران»؛ کتاب سوم «آخرین ستاره»؛<br /><br />سه گانه موج پنجم روایت یورش سنگین بیگانگان به زمین است، چهار موج پیشین زمین را به عصر پارینه سنگی تبدیل کرده، و انسانها و مردمان بسیاری را از بین برده است؛ «کیسی سالیوان» شانزده ساله، در تلاش است تا برادر کوچکترش را از تازش مرگبار بیگانگان، در برابر «موج پنجم» زنده نگهدارد؛ و ...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1088825623" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088825623" />

<div id="review_1254577608" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1254577608" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1254577608?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=apocalyptic-post-apocalytic">apocalyptic-post-apocalytic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1254577608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12240867679679587038"><br/>I doubt the finale of this supposedly epic series is meant to be funny but if there’s anything the book achieved, it’s that it really was funny- the cheesy kind, hundreds of eye-rolls worthy kind of funny but funny nonetheless. <b>“Ben, Has-Ben and What-Might-Have-Ben”</b> really cracked me up in the cheesiest way possible. But is it just me or did anybody else notice that change in tone because I couldn’t seem to recall Cassie this funny or even Ben for that matter. I guess the end of the world makes </span>
  <span id="freeText12240867679679587038" style="display:none"><br />I doubt the finale of this supposedly epic series is meant to be funny but if there’s anything the book achieved, it’s that it really was funny- the cheesy kind, hundreds of eye-rolls worthy kind of funny but funny nonetheless. <b>“Ben, Has-Ben and What-Might-Have-Ben”</b> really cracked me up in the cheesiest way possible. But is it just me or did anybody else notice that change in tone because I couldn’t seem to recall Cassie this funny or even Ben for that matter. I guess the end of the world makes survivors comediennes/comedians. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“You know you’ve reached a very sad place when the only person who can make you laugh is yourself.” </b>
</i><br /><br />*Guess I’m in a very, very sad place right now, tsk, tsk.*<br /><br />But even though I did enjoy the humor and sarcasm, Cassie felt like a totally different person here with all her cheesy and snarky narrations. It’s the end of the world and there Cassie goes writing tacky, personal fantasies in her journal while Ben uses his one thousand kilowatt killer smile as weapon against the enemy or the girl he desires. *eye-roll times 1000*<br /><br />I only kept reading on because I needed my closure but without that resolve, I doubt I’d have the strength to finish the novel because half of the time I was pretending to understand the mess that is the plot and the other half, I was rolling my eyes over the unwise decisions of the characters, of the absurdity of the whole Fifth Wave concept and over the unresolved conflicts within and among the characters. <br /><br /><b>***Not really a spoiler but may be interpreted as a spoiler by some so read at your own risk***</b><br /><br />And because this is a post apocalyptic trilogy, aside from the many characters that kept dying since the first book, somebody really important had to die. It’s now your job to find who that is which isn’t exactly a very difficult task because the clues are all over the place. Jeez! Initially I thought it gave the story poetic justice but after I read everything, my only thought was: What’s the point?! <br />Uncle Ricky, you owe me big time. :(<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12240867679679587038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
