<div id="review_623601871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623601871" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/623601871?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=tearjerkers">tearjerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=author-betrayal">author-betrayal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer623601871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9076565557416898531"><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Call me Zombie.<br/>Everything hurts. Even blinking hurts. But I’m getting up. That’s what zombies do.<br/>We rise.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/><br/>Okay so…I’m not guna lie. I had a review that I LOVED written out, but my laptop is acting up again and it shut off before my USB saved it. I was going to recreate it, I was in the process of doing so, but it seems stupid. Those were REAL emotions and they flowed out of me so easily…but <b>that’s what happens when you <i>truly</i> connect with a story</b>. So, seeing as I loved this story, this</span>
  <span id="freeText9076565557416898531" style="display:none"><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Call me Zombie.<br>Everything hurts. Even blinking hurts. But I’m getting up. That’s what zombies do.<br>We rise.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>Okay so…I’m not guna lie. I had a review that I LOVED written out, but my laptop is acting up again and it shut off before my USB saved it. I was going to recreate it, I was in the process of doing so, but it seems stupid. Those were REAL emotions and they flowed out of me so easily…but <b>that’s what happens when you <i>truly</i> connect with a story</b>. So, seeing as I loved this story, this series, these characters with all my heart, I made a connection so strong, so unyielding that I have a lot to say. Too much to say. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>So there you go. You can love the good in us and hate the bad, but the bad is in us, too. Without it, we wouldn’t be us.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_n1q7qgKjhr1r9h6gko1_500_zps3gu3uely.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441290744ra/16089575.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_n1q7qgKjhr1r9h6gko1_500_zps3gu3uely.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So, instead of trying to recreate those raw emotions, this amazing idea I had explaining how beautiful bookends could be (you’d have <i>totally</i> dug it, guyz-as it is, this makes no sense. Had you read my profound thoughts in said erased review, you’d have been all…wow, that makes sense. Obvi), I’m going to go a different direction. Write a wholly different review with another set of raw emotions…because that just proves to you how much this book and series meant to me. A whole review of epic, wonderful, well-thought out things I bared from my soul are gone forever with no ounce of documentation…and I’m barely upset. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>I’ll kill until I lose count. I’ll kill until counting doesn’t matter.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>Sure, I’m angry, I loved what I did. But, as it is, I could never say everything I’m thinking in one review, so another take on my thoughts couldn’t hurt. It’s just not the same. Anyway. <b>My feels know no bounds</b>. Sorry I rambled. Sorry I’ve been thinking about this since I finished 24 hours ago. Sorry I have re read my quotes over and over and over and over again…and <b>I still break down every time</b>. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_nzkty841Yq1u7gnm9o1_500_zpsa1psuxp7.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464701243ra/19266081.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_nzkty841Yq1u7gnm9o1_500_zpsa1psuxp7.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>It’s more than Zombie can handle. He falls against the side of the barricade, gulping air, his face lifted up to the sky. Lost, found, dead, alive, the cycle repeats; there’s no escape, there’s no reprieve. Zombie closes his eyes and waits for his breath to slow, his heart to steady. A small break before it begins again: the next loss, the next death.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>It’s not often I love a whole series from beginning to end. It’s a rarity. Authors start out these series with promising ideas, wonderful, charismatic characters, and the question of what’s to come for everything involved. We wait and we wait and we wait…Because no matter how much we beg and plead and cry for the next book, it’s all a fruitless endeavor, isn’t it? They do what they want anyway, right? Especially those last books…they love to pull those final book extensions because <i> 'You want it to be what it’s meant to be right? You don’t want it messed up. We’re doing this to give you the best story possible. Don’t you want the perfect end to your beloved series??? You wouldn’t want to ruin that, would you?’</i> So they tweak and they twist and they turn and they add and delete and edit edit edit and they don’t release it until they are damn well ready to.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>She was the mayfly, here for a day, then gone. She was the last star, burning bright in a sea of limitless black. </blockquote>
</b><br><br>So…we sit again. We wait. And then it appears on our e-readers or on our doorstep and we immediately download it at midnight and read and read and read and then it’s like…that’s <i>it</i>? This is the end we waited for? Not everyone gets as disappointed, haughty, or judgmental as I, though, apparently, because there have been, like, seven releases this year for finales and I’ve hated 6 out of the 7 while others loved them. It’s been rather…devastating. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I supposed I could turn to Bear. It was always easy to talk to him. We had hours of conversation, <i>good</i> conversation, during those weeks when it was just me and him hiding in the woods. Bear’s an excellent listener. He never yawns or interrupts or walks away. Never disagrees, never plays games, never lies. <i>I go where you go, always</i>, that’s Bear’s jam.<br>Bear proves that true love doesn’t have to be complicated-or even reciprocated.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>So when I saw this was close to <i>finally</i> being released (DAMN YOU, YOU STUPID 8 (or however many) month set back!) I was blasé about it. What did I even have to look forward to, ya know??? <b>I have hated almost every series end this year</b> and have been living in heartbreak hotel all by my lonesome as each bbf’s story crumbled to ashes. And then this little morsel appeared on my iPad. My hopes were low, I didn’t set the bar too high….but anyone that knows me knows this was a defense mechanism. <b>I have loved this series since it was first released years ago</b>. I have followed Cassie on her journey from the very beginning as she chased after Sammy, held that damnable teddy bear, found a deep bond with an otherworldly sniper, and her teenage crush. She has been through the ringer (HA! That bitch….) and only <b>wants to make a world where her little brother can live and see it as she has gotten to</b>. See the universe’s beauty, the stars, the sky. Birds and rivers and schools and friendship and love. Not devastation, war, battling to wake up each day alive, fighting for each breath earned. Not needing to hold up a gun at every stranger lest they rip you to shreds or shoot your head off before you get a chance to. A world with trust. A world with unity. A world with peace and kindness….a world with hope. <b>A world like <i>before</i></b>.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>And I run on. Through a primordial landscape unscarred by any human thing, the world as it was before trust and cooperation unleashed the beast of progress. The world is circling back now to what it was before we knew it. Paradise lost. Paradise returned.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/Cassiopeia-A_zpsoiuqvuoq.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464701243i/19266082._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo Cassiopeia-A_zpsoiuqvuoq.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>This. Book. Was. Everything.</b> It was rain clouds and sunshine and laughter and friendship and sacrifice and loyalty. It was every moment. It was every thought. It was your waking breath and your final memory before sleep. It was your dreams and your consciousness and it was….<i>everything</i>.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>But the most wonderful thing of all, our highest achievement and the one thing for which I pray we will always be remembered, is stuffing wads of polyester into an anatomically incorrect, cartoonish ideal of one of nature’s most fearsome predators for no other reason than to soothe a child.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I was prepared for x. I was prepared for xx. I was even prepared for xxx….but what I didn’t expect, what I wasn’t ready for…<b>I wasn’t prepared for <i>this</i></b>. How does an author…do this? I can’t explain it. In no way can it be described. It’s like…you know you’re hungry, but you aren’t sure what you feel like. So you kind of just…chill. Take it all in, decide to go for the ride and see what you feel like in a minute. And then all of a sudden someone hands you something or you see a meal come out in front of you and it just…<i>clicks</i>. <i>That</i> is what you want, and it is exactly what you needed-You just didn’t know it. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Reduce the human population to a sustainable number, then crush the humanity out of it, since trust and cooperation are the real threats to the delicate balance of nature, the unacceptable sins that drove the world to the edge of a cliff.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>And that’s this story. This trilogy had integrity from the start. Whether you liked, hated, or loved, no one could say it lacked originality or that it didn’t pique your curiosity. I mean, everyone can agree on that, right? <b>I’m real big on integrity</b>, and I’ve been super upset this year that so many series have lost their…spark, their originality. They have lost the thing that makes them so special and what made them stand out among all the other series, in my mind. But this series…from book one on, I have been nothing but awed. Nothing but impressed. <b>The second book got dark</b>, therefore making me even more of a fan, even as some people dwindled off and lost their love for it. Hey, you can’t win with everyone. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Lying is like murder-after the first one, each one that follows is easier.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>But then this was released….and I can’t even explain how perfectly <i>perfect</i> this was wrapped up. And here’s the most beautiful thing about it: <b>It wasn’t wrapped up in a neat little bow</b>. BOOM. I just…YES. Thank you!!! These dystopian authors think that their crumbling world has to be put back together in the end, that the world could so easily be re-made, rebooted, whatever. But no. Fuck that. Life is messy. The world is messy. <i>We</i> are messy. Humanity has been ripped from all these people and we expect it all to be fixed by a few action scenes? I don’t think so. And Yancey didn’t even try to pull that shit. <b>Each scene was a building block</b> and a new layer on an intricately pieced together puzzle, and until that final sentence, that final paragraph, that final <i>moment</i>…nothing fit. And that’s the most amazing, mesmerizing, breath-taking thing to me: <b>It was perfectly imperfect</b>….and therein lies the integrity. Loads and loads of integrity…and I am utterly speechless about it. (Well…)<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Why must I always be the isle of crazy alone in an ocean of sensibility? The <i>should</i> to everybody else’s <i>shouldn’t</i>? The <i>I-will</i> to their <i>better-nots</i>?</blockquote>
</b><br><br><br><b>I couldn’t breathe from beginning to end</b>. My heart was beating faster and faster with each progressing page. My mind was racing at the speed of light, trying it’s fucking hardest to figure out what was going to happen, who would make it (would anyone make it?), how it would end, who was worth keeping and who was worth discarding. And…okay, I’ll fucking admit it, who the hell Cassie would be with, in the end. Sorry. Is what it is-but the best part??? THIS STORY. <b>This story was larger than a girl and a boy</b> and another boy and a slightly mean sniper girl-This series and this end <b>made me proud of the dystopian genre</b>, again. This is how you end a series. This is how it’s done. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Squad 53 is gone, broken apart, dead or missing or dying or running.<br>RIP, squad 53.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I don’t remember so much humor, this dark comic relief that Cassie Sullivan possessed, and Ben Parish’s humor and determination to keep things light in the face of certain death. And I know I shouldn’t say it, I know it sounds bleak, but I’d be shorting myself if I didn’t say it: This book has <b>one of the most heartbreaking scenes I’ve ever read</b>. And it’s not what you’d think…but it burns. It burns so good.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>The others concluded that the only way to save the world was to annihilate civilization. Not from without, but from within. The only way to annihilate human civilization was to change human nature.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/9925620_zpsadycwghp.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464701243ra/19266083.gif" alt=" photo 9925620_zpsadycwghp.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I find it important to note, also, that <b>I literally snarled at my husband because of this book</b>. That’s right. At precisely 12:41 AM on the 25th (or was it technically the 26th?) of May, my hubbs woke up and proceeded to try and be suave and play nice and flirt with me once he saw I was awake and I literally, and I do mean LITERALLY, <b>looked over and bared my teeth at him</b> with a very viscous, aggressive, and otherwise very unattractive snarl-scraggly as I was, this did not help. You know, that tangled hair and tears streaming down my face while battling my choking sobs. I might have even been giving a very valiant effort at pulling my hair out. <b>Silly boy, don’t you know not to interrupt the reader</b> while she’s fully submerged in another reality??<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>They wanted a mindless, stone-cold killer to let loose on the world. They wanted a zombie. Now they’ve got one.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>All the feels. All the stars. <b>I was crushed in a way I wasn’t prepared for</b>. And it’s my own fault, really. Because seriously…I was too busy judging my love for all the characters and my emotional investment in them:<br><br><b>Cassie</b>-Can’t remember how I felt before, but OBSESSED with her now<br><b>Evan</b>-Still like but…just not like I used to<br><b>Ben Parish</b>-AGHHHHHH more than I even remember possible!! I WILL LOVE YOU FOREVER, my Zombie!! Protect me! lol<br><b>Ringer</b>-Begrudgingly like, how I’ve pretty much always felt<br><b>Nugget</b>-Oh, Nugget, must you hurt your sister’s feelings, so?? But anyway, love his POV now, whereas I never did before<br><br>Anyway…my point. How could I forget? <b>Humanity comes first, in the end</b>. I HATE YOU, YOU STUPID BOOK. I lie. I love you so much. Come…come join your friends on the bookshelf… <br><br><br><br><br><br>More quotes I didn't get to put in (if you wana read them :P):<br><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I stood up. Then I sat back down. There was nowhere to go. Well, I could go to the kitchen and make a sandwich, except there was no bread or deli meat or cheese. I don’t know the particulars, but I’m pretty sure there’s a Subway on every corner in heaven. Also Godiva stores. On our second day here, I found Grace’s stash of forty-six boxes of Godiva chocolates. Not that I counted them.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>After Sam hit me on the nose, I burst out of the bathroom, soaking wet, whereupon I smacked into Ben Parish’s chest. Ben was lurking in the hallway as if every little thing that has to do with Sam is his responsibility, the aforesaid little shit screaming obscenities at my back, the only dry part of my body after trying to wash his, and Ben Parish, the living reminder of my father’s favorite saying that it’s better to be lucky than smart, gave me that ridiculous <i>what’s up?</i> look, so stupidly cute that I was tempted to break <i>his</i> nose, thereby making him not so damn Ben Parish-y looking.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Stopping just short of the doorway, I pull out one of the stun grenades. I slip my finger into the pin. My hands are shaking. A dribble of sweat courses down the middle of my back. This is how they get you, this is how they crush the spirit right out of you. Out of the blue the past is rammed down your throat, a gut punch of memories of all the things you took for granted, the things that you lost in the blink of an eye, the stupid, trivial, forgettable things you didn’t know could crush you, things like an old woman’s quivery voice, high-pitched and far away, calling you inside for a plate of warm cookies and a glass of ice-cold milk. </blockquote>
</b><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

</a> <br><br><br>Wow. I'm...actually speechless. <b>My heart</b>...is that my heart ripped to shreds on the floor?<br><br>I don't know what to say. I don't know how to process [all the epic]. <br><br>I am a walking, talking ZOMBIE and I definitely didn't sleep last night.<br><br>Zombie.<br><br><b>Finally</b>. Finally an author who ends a trilogy the way it should be....and I was highly critical-you bet your ass on that. No free 5 star hand out here. Just....I am without words. Can't complete full sentences. <b>I am without emotion</b>. Comatose.<br><br>Yeah. Just call me Zombie. </span>

<div id="review_1058440672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1058440672" />
    <a title="Mario" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16628840-mario"><img alt="Mario" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588674821p2/16628840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1058440672?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario" href="/user/show/16628840-mario">Mario</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1058440672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14836782254584955283"><i>But I am even more than this. I am all those they remember, the ones they loved, everyone they knew, and everyone they only heard about. How many are contained in me? Count the stars. Go on, number the grains of sand. That's me.<br/>I am humanity.</i><br/><br/><br/>Damn, this book completely destroyed me.<br/><br/><i>The Last Star</i> was one of my most anticipated books, if not the most anticipated book, of this year. And because of that, I was really hoping that <i>Yancey</i> would end the trilogy in a nice way, and that the ending wouldn’t</span>
  <span id="freeText14836782254584955283" style="display:none"><i>But I am even more than this. I am all those they remember, the ones they loved, everyone they knew, and everyone they only heard about. How many are contained in me? Count the stars. Go on, number the grains of sand. That's me.<br />I am humanity.</i><br /><br /><br />Damn, this book completely destroyed me.<br /><br /><i>The Last Star</i> was one of my most anticipated books, if not the most anticipated book, of this year. And because of that, I was really hoping that <i>Yancey</i> would end the trilogy in a nice way, and that the ending wouldn’t suck. And now that I’ve read it, I can safely say that <i>Yancey</i> ended the book in an amazing way. I was still left wanting more, but at the same time I’m satisfied with the way the book ended. <br /><br />Now moving on to the plot. From the beginning, I loved the places the story went. I loved that we got multiple points of view, and that we heard from every main character evenly. Unlike the second book, which focused mostly on Ringer, this one focused on every main character. Speaking of characters: Cassie, Evan and Ringer continued to be my favorites (Cassie, especially). I loved her sense of humor, and I enjoyed reading from her point of view the most. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that's why the way Yancey ended her story hit me so damn hard <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I also loved that this book referenced many quotes and events from the first book, and that we kind of got a closure to those events and quotes.<br /><br />I should probably now stop, before I start rambling. All in all, I loved this whole trilogy, and I was satisfied with the ending (even though it left me feeling sad and depressed, the ending was still beautiful). If you haven’t still started this series I would genuinely recommend starting it, because it truly is amazing, and it is easily going into my 'all time favorite trilogies' list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14836782254584955283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1277394500?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who seek the depth of human philosophy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=never-read-it-again">never-read-it-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=just-fine">just-fine</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1277394500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16552774382015775867"><b>
  <u>Latest Update: 24/05/2017</u>
</b><br/>GUYS!!!! Do you know that there'll be three new books based on The 5th Wave trilogy??? The next installment will be out in spring, 2018!!! Read the announcement <a href='http://www.denofgeek.com/us/books-comics/the-5th-wave/262860/rick-yancey-to-publish-three-more-5th-wave-books' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a>!!!!<br/><br/>Although I disliked the ending of this one, now I have high hope for a better one *FINGERS AND TOES CROSSED* !!! What do you think? Are you excited about it? Please let me know! :D<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Review: 11/09/2016</u>
</b><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>They rest in us and we in them. Our heart contains all others. One heart, one life, on the a</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16552774382015775867" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Latest Update: 24/05/2017</u>
</b><br />GUYS!!!! Do you know that there'll be three new books based on The 5th Wave trilogy??? The next installment will be out in spring, 2018!!! Read the announcement <a href="http://www.denofgeek.com/us/books-comics/the-5th-wave/262860/rick-yancey-to-publish-three-more-5th-wave-books" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>!!!!<br /><br />Although I disliked the ending of this one, now I have high hope for a better one *FINGERS AND TOES CROSSED* !!! What do you think? Are you excited about it? Please let me know! :D<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Review: 11/09/2016</u>
</b><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>They rest in us and we in them. Our heart contains all others. One heart, one life, on the advent of a mayfly's final flight.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />After finishing the book(huh, finally), I felt like being brainwashed over and over again so all you need to know what this book's about is that <u>
  <b>WE ARE HUMANITY AND WE ARE ONE</b>
</u>. Why does it sound like a <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TGtWWb9emYI" rel="nofollow noopener">song</a>? <br /><br />In the first 288 pages, it's just a story about small kids holding sidearms and guns like a teddy bear; they don't remember ABCs but know how to make bombs; they're a bunch of children who know how to shoot people with green lights around their heads without blinking, annihilate humanity, and change human nature.<br /><br />Everything is utterly twisted here. At first I thought maybe it was inevitable when living in an alien-infested world like that, but later I was like, <i>oh, okay, so people can just kill whoever is in their way and still get a nice sleep at night and no need to feel guilty at all because that's how it works and we just have to adapt.</i> Don't blame me but this is what the book made me.<br /><br />Thus, in my most genuine opinion, I think what's really <b>worthy of reading is the final 50 pages and that's all.</b> You don't necessarily need to know what happened before these pages (and to save your innocent hearts) because like I said, I barely knew what was going on 80% of the book. And still, I managed to <i>understand</i> something (well, that's a bit overestimated) from page 289 to page 338. You'll find the truth about humanity and how mayfly's sacrifice effects the rest of the survivors. Basically, the entire trilogy is all connected, from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_" title="The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The 5th Wave</a> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131484.The_Infinite_Sea__The_5th_Wave___2_" title="The Infinite Sea (The 5th Wave, #2) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Infinite Sea</a> and lastly, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131489.The_Last_Star__The_5th_Wave___3_" title="The Last Star (The 5th Wave, #3) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Star</a>. However, I can assure you that I don't like where the story leads and how it ends. <br /><br />The ending is..., well, I have no words because it reminds me of that of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18710190.Allegiant__Divergent___3_" title="Allegiant (Divergent, #3) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Allegiant</a> in the Divergent series, which I absolutely didn't enjoy. But at the same time, there's no loose end eventually and it's not that bad, either. *I have no idea what I'm talking about because I kind of lost the ability to form a complete thinking after the virtual apocalypse.*<br /><br />Anyway, reading this book is like watching the movie, <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1375666/" rel="nofollow noopener">Inception</a> and reading another book called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1656001.The_Host__The_Host___1_" title="The Host (The Host, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Host</a> in the meanwhile. That's what it is. When you combine their stories together and you'll get <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131489.The_Last_Star__The_5th_Wave___3_" title="The Last Star (The 5th Wave, #3) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Star</a>. Embrace yourself for further confusion and uncertainty. <br /><br />Last but not least, if you decide not to read this one, here's the briefing:<br /><b>1) VQP=Vincit qui patitur (latin)= He conquers who endures.<br />2) We are humanity and we are one. Our name is Cassiopeia.<br />3) Mayfly finally takes flight. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16552774382015775867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1558385354?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Corner" href="/user/show/46088881-reading-corner">Reading Corner</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1558385354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8263452532066282288">This book is a massive let down and a terrible end to a great series.I hated reading most of this book,the whole plot was just so messy and everything was all over the place.The format was annoying,things didn't add up or didn't make sense,the plot was weak and characters seemed so off.<br/><br/>I loved the other two books in <b>The Fifth Wave Series</b>,I was so excited to read <b>The Last Star</b> but the book was terrible compared to the others.It strayed away from everything that made the other books good,there was</span>
  <span id="freeText8263452532066282288" style="display:none">This book is a massive let down and a terrible end to a great series.I hated reading most of this book,the whole plot was just so messy and everything was all over the place.The format was annoying,things didn't add up or didn't make sense,the plot was weak and characters seemed so off.<br /><br />I loved the other two books in <b>The Fifth Wave Series</b>,I was so excited to read <b>The Last Star</b> but the book was terrible compared to the others.It strayed away from everything that made the other books good,there was no atmosphere building,it constantly switched between characters instead of giving one long narrative and it was pretty confusing at times.<br /><br />Parts were gripping but I still found it difficult to really immerse myself into the book because I was usually bored.I began to hate most of the characters like Ben and especially Ringer because they annoyed the shit out of me and Ringer seemed so out of character compared to the previous books.<br /><br />What really ruined <b>The Last Star</b> for me was the atrocious ending,everything was wrapped up so messily with one of the most unfulfilling ends ever.I was just left feeling annoyed and wishing I didn't ruin the series by reading this book.I rated the other books 4.5 stars but I'm only giving this one a 2 because it was a terrible finish to the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8263452532066282288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1368315193" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9079694427242092937"><b>First Read: July 2016, Rating: 4 Stars<br/>Second Read: November 2018, Rating: 4 Stars</b><br/><br/>Well, all I can say is, <b>THIS IS HOW YOU FINISH A SERIES!</b><br/><br/>This is the last, and my absolute favourite, installment in the 5th Wave dystopian series and I am so incredibly sad my journey with Cassie and co. has come to an end! Yancey has created such a stellar cast of characters that overwhelmed me, moved me and had me screaming with both laughter and pain. I became so emotionally invested in their main objective as we</span>
  <span id="freeText9079694427242092937" style="display:none"><b>First Read: July 2016, Rating: 4 Stars<br />Second Read: November 2018, Rating: 4 Stars</b><br /><br />Well, all I can say is, <b>THIS IS HOW YOU FINISH A SERIES!</b><br /><br />This is the last, and my absolute favourite, installment in the 5th Wave dystopian series and I am so incredibly sad my journey with Cassie and co. has come to an end! Yancey has created such a stellar cast of characters that overwhelmed me, moved me and had me screaming with both laughter and pain. I became so emotionally invested in their main objective as well as their individual plights and I think this is in part due to the brilliant construction of their characters as well as the sublime and lyrical quality to the writing. These combined to transcend the confines of the YA genre and create a stunning masterpiece! <br /><br />The whole series is concerned with the question of what humanity exactly is, and I think each individual character and Yancey's creation of them perfectly summed this up: they are humanity. They are real human beings that have evocatively been brought to life and I feel like I have lost a family now this series is sadly at an end!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9079694427242092937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1424802486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10562665638088493142"> <blockquote>
  <i>“Because here’s the thing: seeing yourself through another’s eyes shifts your center of gravity. It doesn’t change the way you look at yourself. It changes the way you look at the world. Not the you. The everything-but-you.” </i>
</blockquote><br/><b>I am so dissapointed in this book/ series.</b><br/><br/> The Last Star was 200 pages of <b>verbosity</b>. I am sorry but it really was.This series started out great, I loved The 5th Wave but it got worse and worse. I still don't understand <b>WHY? Why all this? Why the waves and why the killin</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10562665638088493142" style="display:none"> <blockquote>
  <i>“Because here’s the thing: seeing yourself through another’s eyes shifts your center of gravity. It doesn’t change the way you look at yourself. It changes the way you look at the world. Not the you. The everything-but-you.” </i>
</blockquote><br><b>I am so dissapointed in this book/ series.</b><br><br> The Last Star was 200 pages of <b>verbosity</b>. I am sorry but it really was.This series started out great, I loved The 5th Wave but it got worse and worse. I still don't understand <b>WHY? Why all this? Why the waves and why the killings?</b> This may sounds a bit harsh but this one thing keeps bugging me; The author keeps talking about humanity, hope and humanity all over again, how to kill humanity, how to destroy love blah blah. Okay I get it you're trying to write something <b>DEEP </b>but it's just gets annoying and boring after one point.<br><br> Cassie was unbearable in this book. She kept complaining and getting angry for no reason, basically she acted like a 5 year old whose mom didn't buy her a candy. Evan was like a lost puppy but in a bad way. I didn't care for these two till one certain point. Another flaw in this book is Sam's POV. HE'S A 5 YEAR OLD! He shouldn't be able to think and do the things he does even if the world goes shit around him. Very unrealistic.The only characters that make this book bearble for me is Ringer and Ben Parrish, at least they still rock.<br><br>It will seem funny after all this negative talk however I loved the ending, it almost brought tears to my eyes, <b>almost...</b><br>The 5th wave was really good but after last 2 books I don't know what to think about this series anymore. Sorry...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465238256ra/19329152.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-dystopian">fantasy-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=the-end-of-the-world-as-we-know-it">the-end-of-the-world-as-we-know-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1557257910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5357908656804739025">I feel like this was a satisfying conclusion to the trilogy. We basically pick right up where we left off. Our group is still trying to prevent alienpocalypse (well, that already happened, but they are trying to prevent utter and complete annihilation of the human species, stuff like that). Sometimes they are together and sometimes they have to split up, depending on what the mission is. My favorites were Ringer and Zombie (Ben Parrish). Sam gets a couple POVs. <br/><br/>At first, I felt like I had waited</span>
  <span id="freeText5357908656804739025" style="display:none">I feel like this was a satisfying conclusion to the trilogy. We basically pick right up where we left off. Our group is still trying to prevent alienpocalypse (well, that already happened, but they are trying to prevent utter and complete annihilation of the human species, stuff like that). Sometimes they are together and sometimes they have to split up, depending on what the mission is. My favorites were Ringer and Zombie (Ben Parrish). Sam gets a couple POVs. <br /><br />At first, I felt like I had waited too long between book 2 and 3 and was missing a few things, but I eventually caught on and remembered. Cassie still bugged me, but she actually ended up having heroic moments. <br /><br />There was a lot of action, the pacing felt pretty even. Overall, this kept my interest the whole way through, answered some questions, and was satisfying. I would recommend this trilogy and it has become one of my favorites. But I would read them all, if not back to back, then fairly close together so you don't forget too many details.<br /><br />I could have used a few more answers about the aliens. They still remained pretty vague. But I got enough that it didn't ruin things.<br /><br />Oh, I'm not a huge fan of what was done with Evan Walker's character, but it wasn't a deal-breaker. <br /><br />You aren't going to get all your questions answered and there isn't a typical HEA with a bow tied on top, but there are still some happy endings.<br /><br />BIG SPOILER - don't read if you have not read and intend to!<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was okay with Cassie dying. Usually I hate when authors kill off MCs, but this felt right. It didn't feel like it was done to shock readers. It had to be done. Also, considering she was my least favorite...  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />My reviews for the other books:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16101128.The_5th_Wave__The_5th_Wave___1_" title="The 5th Wave (The 5th Wave, #1) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The 5th Wave</a> #1 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/942982878?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">4 stars</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131484.The_Infinite_Sea__The_5th_Wave___2_" title="The Infinite Sea (The 5th Wave, #2) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Infinite Sea</a> #2 - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1557252503?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">3 stars</a><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5357908656804739025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1650380628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1650380628" />
    <a title="Beth Hudspeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18107143-beth-hudspeth"><img alt="Beth Hudspeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495723320p2/18107143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1650380628?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Hudspeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Hudspeth" href="/user/show/18107143-beth-hudspeth">Beth Hudspeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=cant-wait-2016">cant-wait-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18107143-beth-hudspeth?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650380628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2889821113573726811"><b>Reviewed by</b>: <a href='https://hellobeautifulbookblog.com/2016/06/13/book-review-the-last-star-by-rick-yancey/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hello Beautiful Book Blog</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Yancey is back at it again with precise characterization, fierce energy, and an eerie awareness that time is running out.</i>
</b><br/><br/>The Last Star… The. Last. Star.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Love is forever. If it wasn’t, it wouldn’t be love. The world is beautiful. If it wasn’t, it wouldn’t be the world.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>How do I put into words how much I was anticipating this book? I think it’s impossible. I was so engrossed with The 5th Wave. I love YA and I am such a sucker for YA trilogies, don’t as</span>
  <span id="freeText2889821113573726811" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by</b>: <a href="https://hellobeautifulbookblog.com/2016/06/13/book-review-the-last-star-by-rick-yancey/" rel="nofollow noopener">Hello Beautiful Book Blog</a><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Yancey is back at it again with precise characterization, fierce energy, and an eerie awareness that time is running out.</i>
</b><br /><br />The Last Star… The. Last. Star.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Love is forever. If it wasn’t, it wouldn’t be love. The world is beautiful. If it wasn’t, it wouldn’t be the world.”</i>
</blockquote><br />How do I put into words how much I was anticipating this book? I think it’s impossible. I was so engrossed with The 5th Wave. I love YA and I am such a sucker for YA trilogies, don’t ask me why because I don’t know, but they are my favorite. It felt like I had to wait for ages to get this book AND I actually purchased it because my library had a wait list of <b>22 PEOPLE</b>! I couldn’t wait for months to read what happens! Whatever, it was worth it.<br /><br />I have been trying to process what happened for a while now. It’s something BIG. I really didn’t see this coming until right before, and that’s all I will say about it. Moving on…<br /><br />The story kind of starts out a bit slow and weird. It took me a minute to get back into Yancey’s writing and the world. I did not reread the other 2 books like I would normally do before the finale in a series. I really just didn’t have the time, but after a few chapters I melted right back into the story. After I got my footing, the story really picked up for me. There are so many different elements going on, but mostly it is just scrictly survival. I feel like the story has progressed SO much since The 5th Wave. I don’t really feel like the characters are even the same people after all they have been through.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“We bear the unbearable. We endure the unendurable. We do what must be done until we ourselves are undone.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Yancey has to cover so much and so many POVs in one book that I think some of the smaller details in the characters I loved so much was lost in translation. There is a sort of shift in character focus from The 5th Wave to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131484.The_Infinite_Sea__The_5th_Wave___2_" title="The Infinite Sea (The 5th Wave, #2) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Infinite Sea</a> and then to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131489.The_Last_Star__The_5th_Wave___3_" title="The Last Star (The 5th Wave, #3) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Star</a>. I feel so connected to all of them and that rarely happens.<br /><br />A lot of the time with trilogies I get so engrossed in the first novel because it is all new. I’m learning new worlds, new customs, learning about new characters, and everything in between. Then, by the last book I feel a sort of complacency or almost predictability. That was pretty much the case with this series as well, except there were still some things that shocked me. I had a couple of wide eyed moments and some moments I’m still in disbelief from.<br /><br />I don’t have a whole lot to say about the plot because most of what I would say is just emotions and it’s hard to portray those correctly in words. One thing that is absolutely certain, Rick Yancey has a way with words. I am always captivated by the way he can word things. He can take the barest of sentences and make them sounds amazing.<br /><br />This book is some of what I expected with a lot of the unexpected thrown in. The superb storytelling and the wonderful characters made this series worthwhile for me.<br /><br />I am humanity.<br /><br />Love conquers all.<br /><br />I felt a little numb at first, but now my heart is breaking.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“But I am even more than this. I am all those they remember, the ones they loved, everyone they knew, and everyone they only heard about. How many are contained in me? Count the stars. Go on, number the grains of sand. That’s me.<br />I am humanity.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />♥<br /><br /><br /><br /> <br /><br />*************Spoiler thoughts/questions below***********<br /><br />♥<br /><br />♥<br /><br />♥<br /><br />♥<br /><br />♥<br /><br />I’m still a little confused about who caused/did all of this or I guess more why they did this. Who was the sole person who orchestrated this? Like who created the 12th system? Who are these advanced humans who were able to create it?<br /><br />*********<br /><br />Still trying to process this... be back later.<br /><br />Review to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2889821113573726811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1249285352" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249285352" />
    <a title="Taylor of Elfhame ❦" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38570248-taylor-of-elfhame"><img alt="Taylor of Elfhame ❦" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603671693p2/38570248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249285352?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor of Elfhame ❦" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor of Elfhame ❦" href="/user/show/38570248-taylor-of-elfhame">Taylor of Elfhame ❦</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249285352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14422140497040907093">Alright so... I'm basically forcing myself to write this review because I really just want to put these books behind me. Overall, the only thought I am 100% certain of is "what the everloving fuck was that?" That's it. That's all I really have. So obviously writing a coherent review is a challenge. Try to bear with me. <br/>Sigh.<br/>I loved the Fifth Wave. The first novel was great, not quite a 5 star but very close. It was kick ass with really compelling tone and setting and all these intense little fee</span>
  <span id="freeText14422140497040907093" style="display:none">Alright so... I'm basically forcing myself to write this review because I really just want to put these books behind me. Overall, the only thought I am 100% certain of is "what the everloving fuck was that?" That's it. That's all I really have. So obviously writing a coherent review is a challenge. Try to bear with me. <br>Sigh.<br>I loved the Fifth Wave. The first novel was great, not quite a 5 star but very close. It was kick ass with really compelling tone and setting and all these intense little feelings that had shivers down your spine and suspicion rising in your gut. The second book was less so.... it had something I at the time deemed second book syndrome and therefore I excused a lot of the "um... what?" moments and tried to just invest myself in the characters as I had the first go 'round. It worked somewhat, as I came out of it with a mostly positive experience. It was all very up in the air, mostly because, well, I still had hope. That's the best way I can put it. When the second book lets you down a bit you have hope that the conclusion will set everything right, that it will bring back those feelings of oh god what's going to happen next I have to keep reading I need answers I need more. <br>The Last Star did <b>NOT</b> do that. Like. At all. I barely got through it. I didn't want to read until dawn broke across the sky and I was finished. I didn't want to read until I knew I needed sleep and had a difficult decision to make. No. What I wanted to do was DNF it. I would force myself to read until I reached my daily quota for irritation/confusion and then put it down. Or throw it at the damn wall. No, the second thing. I <b>really</b> wanted to throw this book at the wall. At least once every 50 pages or so. <br>Speaking of pages: does anyone else feel like this series could have been two books? Did we need three books to tell this story? really? I don't feel like it. Everything that happened in books two and three could have been condensed into an around 550 page novel and that could have been the end of it. Because this <b>dragged.</b><br>Alright. Alright. I should probably start getting into detail about the actual book itself now. So <b>SPOILERS</b> from this point on. <br>Ehem. If I may just say:<br><b>RINGER MAKES NO GODDAMN SENSE!!</b> <br>None. And I know, I know that lots and lots of fans absolutely love this girl. I know that. But I'm sorry man, her logic is fucked up eight ways from Sunday 25/9. I don't understand her. I don't understand any of the decisions she made or why or her preachy gospel shit about how she just knows every fucking thing and everyone else is the problem. No Ringer. You, you are the problem. No one gets anything you're talking about because nothing you do makes sense. <br>let's go through Ringer's greatest hits shall we?<br>- Novel starts and she's working for Vosh. Listens to Vosh like his explanations are actually explanations. Ringer, this is the asshole that killed noImnotgonnasaythenumber people. Everyone. How can anything he say possibly excuse that??? But somehow she lets him convince her to kill Evan. And yeah, yeah I know what you're gonna say: <i>but Taylor, Vosh wanted him captured and that's why Ringer wanted him dead so Vosh couldn't have him.</i> <br>This changes nothing. <br>For how smart she claims to be, she never stops to think about one side vs. the other. She never stops to think about humans at all. She doesn't consider that just <b>maybe</b> Evan's 'error' or whatever is bad for Vosh because it is <b>good for humans!</b><br><br><i>Walker is the linchpin, the fulcrum upon which our survival rests. Alive, he is an unacceptable risk.</i><br><br>Uhhhhhhhhh..... WHY?!<br>Seems to me that she might consider that since Vosh=bad and Vosh sees an error in Evan that Evan would therefore = good. So yeah Ringer, let's kill him because what's the point when:<br><br><i>Long after the last human being crumbles to a handful of dust, it will be there, implacable, impenetrable, unknowable. God has been dethroned.</i><br><br>Just how am I supposed to interpret that?? She's operating like everyone is already dead. No fight. No heart. No desperate last hope that <b>maybe</b> there is some way they can all live. She's given up so she goes to kill Evan so everyone else left can see the error of their hopeful ways and give up too. That's what it felt like to me. And it was soooooo annoying. Every time Ringer's pov came up I wanted to stop reading especially bad. But anyway, I was talking about her greatest hits. Ah yes, <br>- bringing a Silencer directly to the people she supposedly cared about. <br>- Pregnancy. Was I the only one who forgot that she even slept with Razor? I still can't even remember when it happened. Maybe you had to squint really hard. Like when Cassie and Evan had sex (I will just revert to my natural reaction: sigh.) You had to squint really hard for that one too. And then you regretted squinting. So all in all when Ringer said those two words my initial reaction (after sighing) was "wait what?" I still don't know why or how her being pregnant contributed to anything at all. I mean... she named the baby after Cassie and we all sniffed for a sec. But beyond that: ???<br>- Suddenly wants to kill Vosh. Um... you were literally <b>just</b> with him. And the whole 'creator' thing just got weirder from there too. <br>I have to stop talking about Ringer. This whole review has been about Ringer and honestly it's giving me a headache. <br>Moving on.<br>Cassie. What on God's green earth even happened to Cassie? And I mean this in two ways. I mean prior-Cassie and noImnotgonnasaythenumber-Cassie. Let's start with prior-Cassie. In the good old days (aka book 1) this girl was kick ass and determined and relatable and all that other good stuff you find in a heroine. Where did that go? Because it wasn't here. Now, I liked Cassie and Evan's relationship. I'm gonna be honest. But this? This was not that. This was... a whole other something that I have a hard time understanding (HA! Kind of like everything else!) All Cassie seemed to do with her POVs was think about boys. Evan and Ben. aw shucks Evan and what-might-have-Ben. Girl. What are you doing? This is the fucking apocalypse! I... andthatsexscenewastrash but anyways. <br>Now for noImnotgonnasaythenumber-Cassie. <br>um......<br><br><a href="http://s1226.photobucket.com/user/ohtruepairings/media/image1%203_zpsc5v8esjl.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464399684ra/19235371.gif" alt=" photo image1 3_zpsc5v8esjl.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>No really. What the fuck? You expect me to believe that the memories of aaaallllllll those people can be put inside one human brain and that human will still be sane enough to do the kind of shit she did afterwards? What? That's not even... Just.<br>And let's not forget Cassie dying. I was supposed to be distraught yes? So sad. Sad enough to cry probably. Nope. I just ... couldn't. Because it was <b>soooooooooooooooo</b> predictable. I'm sad she died, I'm sad about all of them. But really? How typical. It made me more angry than sad. <br>And now Evan. Ah yes, Evan. Everyone-wants-me-dead-because-I-learned-to-love-like-humans-are-<b>supposed</b>-to Evan. I went into this with Evan as my favorite character. Needless to say I was disappointed here as well. All Evan was in this entire book was target practice. What did he actually do? I can't think of anything. Oh wait. He went out and gave himself up to that squad to save Cassie. And then he got turned into a drone and tried to kill her. Anything else? Nope. Target practice. <br>I won't talk about Sam because all he did was annoy the fuck out of me. Please sit the fuck down <i>corporal</i> you're six. Smh. This is not how six year old's think. I can't even put into words how unrealistic. I just can't. <br>Ben was the only acceptable person in this book. The shit he did I understood. He had common sense, dedication, love, basic human decency, hope. I never cared for Ben much in books one and two. But in this one he provided much needed relief from everyone else. <br>My thoughts on the plot?<br>Hmmm...<br>Drinking game. Every time you see the words 'seven billion' take a shot. Hangover will be <i>100</i><br>That's all I got man. That's all I got. <br>So this review turned out to be a lot more negative than originally planned. My rating stays at 3 stars. I'm sorry I just can't give it more. I want to give it less, but I am a generous person. (After further thought turns out I'm not quite generous enough. 1.5 stars it is... I still almost feel like that's being nice.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14422140497040907093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer12713265489097583864">This was 352 pages of pure adrenaline. <br/><br/>This book exceeded my expectations. From beginning to end, it's non-stop, <i>my heart might literally beat out of my chest</i>, action. I'm telling you, you'll fear the lives of every single character. And I don't mean you'll fear their lives, knowing they're meaningless threats.   <span id="freeText12713265489097583864" style="display:none">This was 352 pages of pure adrenaline. <br /><br />This book exceeded my expectations. From beginning to end, it's non-stop, <i>my heart might literally beat out of my chest</i>, action. I'm telling you, you'll fear the lives of every single character. And I don't mean you'll fear their lives, knowing they're meaningless threats. No, it was a genuine fear that constantly kept me on edge.<br /><br />It's been a long time since I've felt completely satisfied with a finale. There's always <i>something</i> that irritates me. I'm tired of seeing stories that wrap up conveniently in a pristine, tidy bow. Regardless of an alien apocalypse, everything is not always perfect. <b>That's life</b>. And that's what I loved about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16131489.The_Last_Star__The_5th_Wave___3_" title="The Last Star (The 5th Wave, #3) by Rick Yancey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Star</a>. It was honest. It was bold. It was perfect.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11873446057372627028">Over all, I don't really know how to feel about this book, or the entire series as a whole. I definitely liked the ending of this one, and the writing was still beautiful, but for the most part I just didn't really care anymore, about most of the characters (they mostly would just annoy me, and is it just me or did Cassie somehow feel oddly... different from the other books?   <span id="freeText11873446057372627028" style="display:none">Over all, I don't really know how to feel about this book, or the entire series as a whole. I definitely liked the ending of this one, and the writing was still beautiful, but for the most part I just didn't really care anymore, about most of the characters (they mostly would just annoy me, and is it just me or did Cassie somehow feel oddly... different from the other books? Her evolution in the middle section was just strange.) and the story in general because, looking back now after having experienced the ending, it just feels like after the first book, the whole narrative took kind of a weird, pointless turn and only came full circle on those last 40 pages, which were undoubtedly pretty incredible. But still, I feel really unsatisfied because even though I wasn't expecting any straight-forward answers, some more clues as to what actually happened would have been nice. I don't know, I probably won't give it too much thought now. Still glad I managed to finish another series, though!</span>

<div id="review_641545533" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/641545533" />
    <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters"><img alt="Trina (Between Chapters)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530495507p2/9323164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/641545533?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trina (Between Chapters)" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters">Trina (Between Chapters)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer641545533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2001872911690226611">I really enjoyed seeing the outcome of this series. This book definitely built upon things that had happened in The Infinite Sea, so in hindsight I can see the purpose that the second book had, although I felt it was a little weak on its own. I had faith it would pay off and I felt it did!<br/><br/>There were a few things I was left confused about, but overall I enjoyed the way that Yancey played with different narratives. He approached the story from several different angles and some events and stylistic</span>
  <span id="freeText2001872911690226611" style="display:none">I really enjoyed seeing the outcome of this series. This book definitely built upon things that had happened in The Infinite Sea, so in hindsight I can see the purpose that the second book had, although I felt it was a little weak on its own. I had faith it would pay off and I felt it did!<br /><br />There were a few things I was left confused about, but overall I enjoyed the way that Yancey played with different narratives. He approached the story from several different angles and some events and stylistic choices in the end lent a really unique reading experience.<br /><br />The change in format was a big improvement. In the first 2 books, each section was narrated by only one character, meaning that we sometimes had to rehash the same events to backtrack to where the new narrative hadn't covered yet. In The Last Star, the sections of the book are now by day instead of character, with many narrative changes happening throughout each section. This created a smooth flow and was a great improvement in my opinion!<br /><br />I did notice 2 cases near the beginning of the book where the narrative changed from past tense to present tense for no reason. I'm sure these were typos. Yancey does use past tense for some characters, present for others, and sometimes a character will narrate using both at different times. Some characters also narrate in first person, while others have a third person narrative. I'm not sure why he chose such variety, but I assume it was to create distinct character voices. I can see how this might be confusing, but I ended up thinking it was an interesting stylistic choice.<br /><br />So, there's a big thing that happens at the end and I'm going to hide it as a spoiler, but want to talk about it! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cassie's death was one of the better treatments of a main character death in YA that I've read. I admit that I didn't find it heart wrenching, but I felt it was handled very well. She made a true sacrifice and showed a real understanding of what she would be facing that was not undermined by surprise villains, immunities, or magic solutions popping up to negate her sacrifice. The plan she carried out had been worked toward and brought about a solution that was truly deserved. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="2001872911690226611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Wm0lDhZPK+ig9HG/5RqZ4JjgHngiIpyLgidZqDqmt/6P1mF+Vn/S1ojZRuUqb/4AD4whKpDC6iwdusQ7R3bAHQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oEOLXPlmc0Psi5cPziTKPka1N6TAMyLINjQBCI5HmWl1+M8suVaKfcSmoFUBUa3e0dkI9nLTVG+pqZyb85fuig==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18104979608670970000">aka Richard Yancey<br/><br/>Rick is a native Floridian and a graduate of Roosevelt University in Chicago. He earned a B.A. in English which he put to use as a field officer for the Internal Revenue Service. Inspired and encouraged by his wife, he decided his degree might also be useful in writing books and in 2004 he began writing full-time.<br/><br/>Since then he has launched two critically acclaimed series: The Ext</span>
  <span id="freeText18104979608670970000" style="display:none">aka Richard Yancey<br /><br />Rick is a native Floridian and a graduate of Roosevelt University in Chicago. He earned a B.A. in English which he put to use as a field officer for the Internal Revenue Service. Inspired and encouraged by his wife, he decided his degree might also be useful in writing books and in 2004 he began writing full-time.<br /><br />Since then he has launched two critically acclaimed series: The Extraordinary Adventures of Alfred Kropp, for young readers, and The Highly Effective Detective, for adults. Both books are set in Knoxville, Tennessee, where Rick lived for ten years before returning to Florida. </span>
